7h2.1044c1.5563,0,2.32,.6206,2.32,1.74,.0109,.539-.2936,1.0349-.7791,1.2692v.0242c.7243,.1716,1.2395,.8131,1.2509,1.5573,0,1.16-.6767,1.9652-2.5133,1.9652h-2.3828v-6.5559Zm2.0483,2.7588c.7414,0,1.1126-.2591,1.1126-.8893,0-.6767-.4456-.899-1.2799-.899h-.6109v1.7883h.7782Zm.2127,2.7898c.87,0,1.362-.2223,1.362-.9261s-.5007-.9667-1.4829-.9667h-.87v1.8908l.9908,.0019Zm4.9406-1.248l-2.32-4.3007h1.4548l1.5418,3.2267,1.6433-3.2248h1.4084l-2.4659,4.2726v2.2775h-1.2566l-.0058-2.2514Z" /></g></g></svg>        </a>
        <div class="me-2">

        <div id="main">
                
    <div class="container article-page py-5">
        <div class="row">
            <div class="col col-lg-8 pe-lg-0">
                                    <div class="article-header">
    <p class="category text-uppercase">ESET Research</p>
    <h1 class="page-headline">Telekopye: Hunting Mammoths using Telegram bot</h1>    <p class="sub-title">Analysis of Telegram bot that helps cybercriminals scam people on online marketplaces</p>
    
    <div class="article-authors d-flex flex-wrap"><div class="article-author d-flex"><a href="/en/our-experts/radek-jizba/" title="Radek Jizba"><picture><source srcset="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/tn/-x45/wls/2023/06/radek_jizba-1.png" media="(max-width: 768px)" /><img class="author-image me-3"  src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/tn/-x45/wls/2023/06/radek_jizba-1.png" alt="Radek Jizba"  /></picture></a><div class="author-text"><p><a href="/en/our-experts/radek-jizba/" title="Radek Jizba"><b>Radek Jizba</b></a></p></div></div></div>
    <p class="article-info mb-5">
        <span>24 Aug 2023</span>
        <span class="d-none d-lg-inline">&nbsp;&bull;&nbsp;</span>
        <span class="d-inline d-lg-none">, </span>
        <span>18 min. read</span>
    </p>

    <div class="hero-image-container">
        <picture><source srcset="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/tn/-x266/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye2.jpeg" media="(max-width: 768px)" /><source srcset="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/tn/-x425/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye2.jpeg" media="(max-width: 1120px)" /><img class="hero-image"  src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/tn/-x700/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye2.jpeg" alt="Telekopye: Hunting Mammoths using Telegram bot"  /></picture>    </div>
</div>
                    <div class="article-body">
    <p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">More and more people nowadays prefer to buy goods online. And why not? It&rsquo;s convenient, goods will be delivered to your doorstep, and if you choose one of many online marketplaces, it&rsquo;s even possible to save some money. Sadly, scammers abuse this, targeting these services and their customers for the scammer&rsquo;s benefit. They can create a listing for goods they don&rsquo;t own or don&rsquo;t intend to sell. Once the victim pays, they seemingly disappear into the ether.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Recently we found the source code of a toolkit that helps scammers so much in their endeavors that they don&rsquo;t need to be particularly well-versed in IT, but only need a silver tongue to persuade their victims. This toolkit is implemented as a Telegram bot that, when activated, provides several easy-to-navigate menus in the form of clickable buttons that can accommodate many scammers at once. In this blogpost we will focus on toolkit analysis and features, and on the structure of the group(s) that use it</span><span class="MsoCommentReference"><span lang="EN-US" style="font-size: 8.0pt;">. </span></span><span lang="EN-US">We have named this toolkit Telekopye.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">This blog post is the first of a two-part series where we take a closer look at Telekopye and show some of the key features that are very helpful to scammers. In the second part, we will focus more on group operations.</span></p>
<blockquote>
<p class="MsoNormal"><strong><span lang="EN-US">Key points of this blogpost</span></strong></p>
<ul>
<li class="Bullets1CxSpFirst"><em><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye is a toolkit that operates as a Telegram bot and helps scammers scam their victims.</span></em></li>
<li class="Bullets1CxSpMiddle"><em><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye is designed to target online marketplaces; mainly (but not exclusively) those popular in Russia.</span></em></li>
<li class="Bullets1CxSpMiddle"><em><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye creates phishing web pages from predefined templates, and </span></em><em><span lang="EN-US">generates and sends phishing emails and SMS messages.</span></em></li>
<li class="Bullets1CxSpLast"><em><span lang="EN-US">Users and operators of Telekopye are organized in a clear hierarchy.</span></em></li>
</ul>
</blockquote>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035925"></a><span lang="EN-US">Overview</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">We devised the name Telekopye as a portmanteau of Telegram and kopye (копье), the Russian word for spear, due to the use of highly targeted (aka spear-) phishing. Victims of this scam operation are called Mammoths by the scammers (see </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">1</span></span><span lang="EN-US">) and several leads point to Russia as the country of origin of the toolkit&rsquo;s authors and users. For the sake of clarity, and following the same logic, we will refer to the scammers using Telekopye as Neanderthals. </span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye meme" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-meme.png" alt="Telekopye meme" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption" style="margin-left: 72.0pt; text-indent: -72.0pt;"><a name="_Ref140045402"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140045402;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">1</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. One of the memes (Mammoth lost) from a group conversation posted by Neanderthals</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal">Telekopye was uploaded to VirusTotal multiple times, primarily from Russia, Ukraine, and Uzbekistan, from where Neanderthals usually operate based on the language used in comments in the code (we have added machine translations to English in brackets in various images in this blogpost) and the majority of targeted markets. Even though the main targets of Neanderthals are online markets popular in Russia, like OLX and YULA, we observed that their targets are also online markets that are not native to Russia, like BlaBlaCar or eBay, and even others that have nothing in common with Russia, like JOFOGAS and Sbazar. Just to illustrate how big some of these marketplaces are, the OLX platform had, <a href="https://fortune.com/2014/10/29/olx-emerging-markets" target="_blank" rel="noopener">according to Fortune</a>, 11 billion page views and 8.5 million transactions per month in 2014.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">We were able to collect several versions of Telekopye, suggesting continuous development. All of these versions are used to create phishing web pages, and send phishing email and SMS messages. In addition, some versions of Telekopye can store victim data (usually card details or email addresses) on disk where the bot is run. Telekopye is very versatile but does not contain any chatbot AI functionality. Hence, it doesn&rsquo;t actually perform the scams; it only eases the generation of content used in such scams. In July 2023, we detected new domains that fit the modus operandi of Telekopye operators, so they are still active. The latest version of Telekopye we have been able to gather was from April 11th, 2022. We assess that Telekopye has been in use since at least 2015 and, based on snippets of conversation between Neanderthals, that different scammer groups are using it.</p>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035926"></a><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye scam scenario</span></h2>
<p class="Bullets1" style="margin-left: 0cm; mso-add-space: auto; text-indent: 0cm; mso-list: none;"><span lang="EN-US">Thanks to human nature, scamming in online marketplaces seems to be very easy. It usually comes down to several key parts of the scam, as seen in Figure 2, that Neanderthals follow. First, Neanderthals find their victims (Mammoths). Then they try to earn their trust and persuade them that they are legitimate (why this is needed we will discuss in part 2). When Neanderthals think that a Mammoth sufficiently trusts them, they use Telekopye to create a phishing web page from a premade template and send the URL to the Mammoth (the URL can also be sent via SMS or email). After the mammoth submits card details via this page, the Neanderthals use these card details to steal money from the Mammoth's credit/debit card, while hiding the money using several different techniques such as laundering it through cryptocurrency. Based on several conversation snippets, we assess that some crypto mixers are involved. There is a missing link between when money is scammed from the Mammoth and the payout to the Neanderthals, which is usually in cryptocurrency.</span><span lang="EN-US"><br /></span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye scam overview" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-scam-overview-with-icon-edited.png" alt="Telekopye scam overview" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref140047451"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140047451;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-no-proof: yes;">2</span></span><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">. </span><span lang="EN-US">Overview of the Neanderthals&rsquo; scam</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035927"></a><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye functionality</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye has several different functionalities that Neanderthals can use to their full extent. These functionalities include sending phishing emails, generating phishing web pages, sending SMS messages, creating QR codes, and creating phishing screenshots. In the following sections, we will focus on the most useful parts of Telekopye for the average Neanderthal.<br /></span></p>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035928"></a><span lang="EN-US">Interface</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal">Every Telegram group using Telekopye consists of one or more Neanderthals that operate simultaneously and independently. Functionality is offered through buttons, likely to make scamming easier for Neanderthals.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Figure 3 shows one of the menus of Telekopye in a working Telegram group. Particularly noteworthy are the buttons &ldquo;My ads&rdquo;, showing all opened listings (ongoing scam advertisements) each Neanderthal has, and &ldquo;My profile&rdquo;, allowing Neanderthals to see their profile information on this platform, such as the number of scams pulled off, amount of money ready for next payout, etc.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye interface" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-buttons.png" alt="Telekopye interface" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref138765417"></a><a name="_Ref138765432"></a><em><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138765417;"><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138765432;"><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138765417;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">3</span></span></span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138765417;"><span lang="EN-US">. Example of Telekopye operator interface</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> in a Telegram group</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035929"></a><span lang="EN-US">Phishing page generation</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal">The core feature of Telekopye is that it creates phishing web pages from predefined HTML templates on demand. A Neanderthal needs to specify the amount of money, product name and, based on the template, additional information like location to which the product will be sent, picture, weight, and buyer&rsquo;s name. Then Telekopye takes all this information and creates a phishing web page. These phishing web pages are designed to mimic different payment/bank login sites, credit/debit card payment gateways, or simply payment pages of different websites.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">To make the phishing website creation process easier, these website templates are organized by countries they target. Figure 4 shows a simple creation menu where some templates are sorted according to different countries. The only outlier is BlaBlaCar for country-independent car-sharing services.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Creation menu" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-scam-choice.png" alt="Creation menu" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref138858839"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138858839;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">4</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Creation menu for different phishing pages. Notice the Swedish flag is incorrectly associated with Switzerland in the top, right corner.</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">5</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> shows one such phishing web page, likely not fully perfected yet.</span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Uncomplete phishing website template" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-unfinished-webpage.png" alt="Uncomplete phishing website template" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref138860332"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138860332;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">5</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Filled in uncompleted phishing website template (machine translations in brackets)</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The finished product is seen in Figure 6, an eBay web page look-alike that is almost unrecognizable from the original (or at least looks like something one would expect from the legitimate website).&nbsp; By clicking the </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">Receive %amount2% EUR</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US"> button, a Mammoth is shown a fake credit/debit card gateway.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Finished template" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-template-example.png" alt="Finished template" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139122359"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139122359;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">6</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. <a name="_Ref139122346"></a>Finished template for phishing web page impersonating eBay</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">These phishing domains are not easy to spot. Usually, Neanderthals register a domain and then create subdomains for each targeted marketplace in such a way that the final URL starts with the expected brand name.</span><span lang="EN-US"> In </span><span lang="EN-US">Table <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">1</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> notice that only one domain <span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">&ndash; </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">olx.id7423[.]ru</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US"> &ndash; is used to target the popular marketplace OLX. An example of a legitimate domain for the OLX marketplace is </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">olx.ua</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. In short, they usually use </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">.ru</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US"> as their top-level domains and move second-level domains to the third-level domain&rsquo;s place.</span></span></p>
<p class="MsoCaption" style="text-align: center;"><em><span lang="EN-US">Table </span><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">1</span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Examples of several domains used for phishing</span></em></p>

<h3><a name="_Toc142035930"></a><span lang="EN-US">Transactions and payout</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Neanderthals do not transfer money stolen from Mammoths to their own accounts. Instead, all the Neanderthals use a shared Telekopye account controlled by the Telekopye administrator. Telekopye keeps track of how successful each Neanderthal is by logging associated contributions to that shared account &ndash; either in a simple text file or a SQL database.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">As a consequence, Neanderthals get paid by the Telekopye administrator. Payment is split into three parts:</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpFirst" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Commission to the Telekopye administrator.</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpMiddle" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Commission to recommender (recommendation system is discussed later in the blog post).</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpLast" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Actual payout.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The commission to the Telekopye administrator is 5&ndash;40%, depending on the Telekopye version and Neanderthal role (roles are also discussed later in the blog post).</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Once a Neanderthal becomes eligible for a payout, he asks Telekopye for one. Telekopye checks the Neanderthal&rsquo;s balance, final request is approved by the Telekopye administrator and, finally, funds are transferred to the Neanderthal&rsquo;s cryptocurrency wallet. In some Telekopye implementations, the first step, asking for a payout, is automated and the negotiation is initiated whenever a Neanderthal reaches a certain threshold of stolen money from successfully pulled off scams (e.g., 500 RUB). The process of the manual payout request is illustrated in Figure 7 and the associated part of the Telekopye source code in Figure 8. </span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Payout diagram" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-payout-diagram-with-icon-edited.png" alt="Payout diagram" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref140047541"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140047541;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-no-proof: yes;">7</span></span><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">.</span><span lang="EN-US"> Payout diagram</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye payout code" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-payout-source.png" alt="Telekopye payout code" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref140832800"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140832800;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">8</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Code that is executed whenever a Neanderthal wants to withdraw funds</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye keeps logs of processed payouts in a separate Telegram channel. A Neanderthal who is paid also receives a link to this channel, probably to be able to verify that the transaction is logged. Figure 9 shows an example of such a logs channel.</span><span lang="EN-US"><br /></span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye payout logs" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-payout-logs.png" alt="Telekopye payout logs" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref138863932"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138863932;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">9</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Example of payout logs in a Telegram channel</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">The Telekopye administrator does not transfer the money through Telekopye itself. Instead, the admin uses either a tool called &ldquo;BTC Exchange bot&rdquo;, likely an independent Telegram bot, or transfers the money manually. However, we have observed increasing integration of payout-related features into Telekopye, so this may change in the future.<br /></span></p>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035931"></a><span lang="EN-US">Sending phishing email<br /></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Neanderthals can instruct Telekopye to create and send email messages. The sender is a predefined email account shared between all the Neanderthals. These email accounts are typically associated with the phishing domains set up by Neanderthals. </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">10</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> shows the code to spoof the email headers </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">From</span></span></span> <span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin;">and </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">Reply-To</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US"> so that the email messages appear more legitimate.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye mail code" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-mail-source.png" alt="Telekopye mail code" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139125896"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139125896;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">10</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Code to craft phishing emails with a fake URL and spoofed sender address</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">11</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> shows one of many templates used to create phishing email bodies. No additional information has been given, so default values are shown, instead of user-defined text, for </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">%title%</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US"> and </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">%amount%</span></span></span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin;">.</span></span><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin;"> A m</span><span lang="EN-US">alicious URL is hidden behind the &ldquo;Go to payment&rdquo; button.</span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye checkout template" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-mail-template.png" alt="Telekopye checkout template" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref138869709"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref138869709;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">11</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Email template that imitates a simple checkout email</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035932"></a><span lang="EN-US">SMS support</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Besides phishing emails, Telekopye allows Neanderthals to create and send SMS messages in a similar manner. </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">12</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> illustrates the piece of code responsible for creating and sending such messages.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye sms code" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-sms-source.png" alt="Telekopye sms code" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139126350"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139126350;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">12</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Part of the code to create SMS messages using the online service [legitimate] smscab.ru</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Some implementations of Telekopye even have predefined SMS texts in different languages. All SMS templates say more or less the same thing, for example, &ldquo;Your item has been paid for. To receive funds, fill out the form: </span><span class="Code"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="font-family: courier new, courier, monospace;">&lt;malicious_link&gt;</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">&rdquo;. Examples of several SMS templates are shown in </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">13</span></span><span lang="EN-US">, where original Russian templates are shown.</span>How this SMS looks when a Mammoth receives it can be seen in Figure 14.</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye sms template text" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-sms-templates.png" alt="Telekopye sms template text" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139126622"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139126622;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">13</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Telekopye SMS template texts in Russian</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye SMS example" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-sms-real.png" alt="Telekopye SMS example" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref140850524"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140850524;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">14</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Example of an SMS created with a template text in Czech and received without a malicious link</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye relies heavily on online services such as smscab.ru or smshub.org to send SMS messages. We have analyzed an older variant, where Telekopye used one hardcoded phone number shared among all Neanderthals. However, likely because blocking one phone number would result in blocking all Neanderthals&rsquo; messages, this feature was discontinued.</span></p>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035933"></a><span lang="EN-US">Image manipulation</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">In this section, we describe how simple it is for Neanderthals using Telekopye to create convincing images and screenshots. Some versions of Telekopye have a component called Render bot. Although Render bot could be classified as a standalone bot, we will handle it as part of Telekopye.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">When Render bot is added to a Telegram chat, we are greeted with the initial message seen in </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">15</span></span><span lang="EN-US">. </span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye initial renderbot message" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-initial-renderbot-message.png" alt="Telekopye initial renderbot message" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139707161"></a><a name="_Ref140213352"></a><em><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139707161;"><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140213352;"><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139707161;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">15</span></span></span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139707161;"><span lang="EN-US">. The initial message from Render bot</span></span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">This gives us good insight into how this part of Telekopye works. We can classify the uses of Render bot into two categories. First, it can be used to mangle images so that they are not easy to cross-reference. Second, it can create fake images that are meant to look like legitimate screenshots. In this section, we will focus first on the creation of these fake screenshots, a feature similar to creating phishing websites.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Unlike fake web pages that are generated from HTML templates, the base for fake screenshots is a JPG image with some key parts removed. These parts include the supposed paid price, debit/credit card number, title, name, etc. This transformation is shown in </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">16</span></span><span lang="EN-US">, where there is a side-by-side comparison of a plain template and a filled template. Because these are images, there are no interactive buttons, unlike the email and phishing web page counterparts.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal">&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Fake screenshot" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-side-by-side-picture-edit.png" alt="Fake screenshot" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139708028"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139708028;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">16</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Generated fake screenshot (template on the left, template filled with sample text on the right)</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">There is a high emphasis on making the inserted text fit as well as possible, so Telekopye supports several different fonts. Just as previously, all behavior is hardcoded and no AI is used. We found nine templates for Sberbank, Avito, Youla, Qiwi, and a few other services.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">From the Neanderthals&rsquo; perspective, creating these screenshots is no different from creating phishing web pages. A Neanderthal only needs to supply a few bits of information, and Telekopye creates a fake screenshot/image from them.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">In Render bot folders it is also possible to see one of these templates in the process of creation. </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">17</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> shows a photo of an invoice for a parcel, with numbered fields. Developers of Telekopye erase all fields with numbers next to them and try to fit their own font style and font size in them. When they are satisfied with how the final product looks, they add it to the bot for other Neanderthals to use as a new template.</span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye invoice" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-invoice.jpeg" alt="Telekopye invoice" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139786435"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139786435;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">17</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Fake check in progress of creation</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Another no less important functionality of this part of Telekopye is image manipulation. From the code and its comments, it is possible to gather that it is able to change images of advertised goods so that search engines cannot cross-reference them. We assume that if the image was found on an online marketplace, AI antispam protection would flag it as malicious. This transformation is very simple and consists of a vertical flip of the image and a small change in contrast.</span></p>
<h3><a name="_Toc142035934"></a><span lang="EN-US">Experimental features</span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Thanks to content from Telekopye source files, we assess that the developers are trying to experiment with different types/variations of the scam. For example, in the code, we see QR code generation functionality (</span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">18</span></span><span lang="EN-US">). This might mean one of two things. Either it is part of the payout process or they are trying to make it a new trick for scamming. A probable reason is that Mammoths don&rsquo;t think twice when paying via a QR code. So we estimate that there is going to be a small increase in scams using these kinds of tricks.</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye QR creation" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-qr-creation.png" alt="Telekopye QR creation" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139784388"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139784388;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">18</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Code that generates QR codes</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">From </span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">15</span></span><span lang="EN-US"> it looks as if Render bot can create fake checks for Sberbank. But in reality, it can only create payment confirmations (</span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">19</span></span><span lang="EN-US">).</span></p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye payout confirmation" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-payout-confirmation.jpeg" alt="Telekopye payout confirmation" width="" height="" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139785357"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139785357;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">19</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Payment confirmation template</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<p class="MsoCommentText"><span lang="EN-US">Fully functioning fake check generation is only a question of time. It is possible to see fragments of work suggesting this is already being worked on. These fragments are mainly handwritten numbers that are probably going to be added as custom fonts. </span></p>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035935"></a><span lang="EN-US">Roles</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Groups of scammers using Telekopye are organized into a hierarchy with least to most privileges in order as follows:</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpFirst" style="margin-left: 14.4pt; mso-add-space: auto; text-indent: -14.4pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Administrators</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpMiddle" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Moderators</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpMiddle" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Good workers / Support bots</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpMiddle" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Workers</span></p>
<p class="Numbering1CxSpLast" style="mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1;"><span lang="EN-US" style="mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-theme-font: minor-latin; color: #0096a1; mso-themecolor: accent2;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">Blocked</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">We have observed some variants enriching this list with a few additions, but these five roles remain the basis. We focus on each role in more detail in the sections below.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Telekopye also employs a referral system. When a new Neanderthal wants to join the group, he needs to fill in an application (how much &ldquo;industry&rdquo; experience he has, who invited him, etc.). This application then needs to be accepted by Moderators or Administrators in order for the new Neanderthal to join.</span><span lang="EN-US"><br /></span></p>
<h3><a name="_Ref139790265"></a><a name="_Toc142035936"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139790265;"><span lang="EN-US">Blocked</span></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">A user with this role is not able to use any part of the Telekopye toolkit. Rules that are part of Telekopye source code suggest this is some sort of punishment for breaking them (</span><span lang="EN-US">Figure <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">20</span></span><span lang="EN-US">).</span></p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<figure class="image"><img title="Telekopye rules" src="https://web-assets.esetstatic.com/wls/2023/2023-8/telekopye-rules.png" alt="Telekopye rules" width="863" height="272" />
<figcaption>
<p class="MsoCaption"><a name="_Ref139127837"></a><em><span lang="EN-US">Figure </span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139127837;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">20</span></span></span><span lang="EN-US">. Rules of Telekopye chat group</span></em></p>
</figcaption>
</figure>
<h3><a name="_Ref139696857"></a><a name="_Toc142035937"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139696857;"><span lang="EN-US">Workers</span></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">This is the most common role that almost all new Neanderthals start with. With this role, Neanderthals are able to use every Telekopye feature, excluding moderation of the group. During payout, this role has the worst commission rates, as seen in </span><span lang="EN-US">Table <span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">2</span></span><span lang="EN-US">.</span></p>
<p class="MsoCaption" style="text-align: center;"><a name="_Ref142038708"></a><em><a name="_Ref142038717"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref142038708;"><span lang="EN-US">Table </span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref142038717;"><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref142038708;"><span lang="EN-US"><span style="mso-no-proof: yes;">2</span></span></span></span><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref142038708;"><span lang="EN-US">. Example of payout rates</span></span></em></p>

<h3><a name="_Ref139696880"></a><a name="_Toc142035938"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139696880;"><span lang="EN-US">Good workers/Support bots</span></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">This role is a direct upgrade of the Worker role. The only difference is that Neanderthals with this role don&rsquo;t have to give such a large percentage of their payout to the platform owner. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">To get this role, Neanderthals must prove their usefulness &ndash; pull off a number of scams or achieve a certain amount of stolen funds.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Sometimes it is possible to see that this role is reserved for support bots. We are not certain what these bots are. </span></p>
<h3><a name="Moderators"></a><a name="_Ref139617978"></a><a name="_Toc142035939"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139617978;"><span style="mso-bookmark: Moderators;"><span lang="EN-US">Moderators</span></span></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><a name="Administrators"></a><a name="_Ref139617998"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: Administrators;"><span lang="EN-US">Moderators can promote and demote other members and approve new members. They cannot modify Telekopye settings.</span></span></p>
<h3><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref139617998;"><span style="mso-bookmark: Administrators;"><a name="_Ref140500266"></a><a name="_Ref140500401"></a><a name="_Toc142035940"></a><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140500401;"><span style="mso-bookmark: _Ref140500266;"><span lang="EN-US">Administrators</span></span></span></span></span></h3>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">Administrators are the highest role in the group. They can use Telekopye to its full extent. On top of moderators&rsquo; capabilities, they can modify Telekopye settings &ndash; add phishing web page templates, change/add email addresses that the bot uses, and change payout rates, payout type, etc.</span></p>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035941"></a><span lang="EN-US">How to avoid being scammed</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal">The easiest way to tell whether you are being targeted by a Neanderthal trying to steal your money is by looking at the language used. It can be the language used in conversation, email, or on the web page itself. Sadly, this is not foolproof, and it has been observed that some of these scam attempts have ironed out grammar and vocabulary mistakes.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Insist on in-person money and goods exchange whenever possible when dealing with secondhand goods on online marketplaces. Such trades are not protected by well-known institutions or services. These scams are only possible because Neanderthals pretend they already paid online/sent an item. Sadly, sometimes in-person delivery is not possible and in that case you need to be extra careful.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Avoid sending money unless you are certain where it will go. When you need to send money somewhere, check the web page for grammatical errors and graphical disproportions. If you are lucky, a template can have some inaccuracies. Also check the website certificate and look closely at the URL, which can be made to look like a real link.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Watch out for strong-arm arguments like &ldquo;I&rsquo;ll send money through service XYZ. Do you know how it works?&rdquo;. Ask if another payment type is possible and especially if they are willing to accept payment from a service you are familiar with. This is not foolproof because scammers have multiple templates, but you might be able to recognize a fake template more easily when you use a payment method known to you.</p>
<p class="MsoNormal">Be extra careful when clicking on links in SMS messages or emails, even if they look as if they come from a reputable source. Neanderthals are no strangers to email spoofing. A good rule of thumb is to ask yourself whether you bought something that would make reputable sources send you emails like that. If you are unsure, visit the supposed service&rsquo;s website directly (not using the link in the email/SMS) and ask. Most of these pages have customer support and they will happily give you a hand.</p>
<h2><a name="_Toc142035942"></a><span lang="EN-US">Conclusion</span></h2>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span lang="EN-US">We discovered and analyzed Telekopye, a toolkit that helps less technical people pull off online scams more easily. We estimate that Telekopye was in use since at least 2015. We focused on one version, analyzing its main capabilities and uncovering how Telekopye works internally. These capabilities include creating phishing websites, sending phishing SMS and emails, and creating fake screenshots. We also described the hierarchy of groups using Telekopye. Thanks to our telemetry, we also found out that this tool is still in use and in active development. The second Telekopye blog post, which will be released later, uncovers the inner working of the scam groups.</span></p>
